Opium Dregs

Are Allowed For International Trade

The Siamese Proposal Was Rejected By The Advisory Committee

Japan And Two Other Countries Abstained

(Geneva) The Opium Advisory Committee discussed the Siamese proposal to allow the import and export of opium dregs today. The debate was extremely fierce and was finally rejected by a vote of fourteen to one. However, Japan and two other countries abstained. (Central News Agency dispatch on the 21st)

(Geneva) The Opium Advisory Committee met this morning to discuss the Siamese government's proposal to legalize the import and export of opium dregs. The Siamese representative said that the proposal was made by the Siamese government alone, stating that the amount of these dregs destroyed each year is extremely large, and there is now a need to use these dregs to manufacture morphine. Siam hopes to transport these dregs to various manufacturing countries, otherwise it will have to establish a morphine manufacturing plant in the country, but it requires a large amount of money. After the Siamese representative finished speaking, he asked the committee for its opinion. Then, the US representative, Mr. Fuller, stood up in a strong tone and said that according to the Hague Convention of 1912, opium dregs must never be imported or exported. The purpose of the Siamese government's proposal is only to seek greater profits than the dregs monopoly. The purpose of the Hague Convention is to gradually prohibit the manufacture, crack down on domestic sales and smoking of cooked opium, and prohibit the international sale of opium dregs. If the use of this sale is allowed, the public sale of opium will continue to exist, and the complete realization of the purpose of the convention will be delayed. The only reason put forward by the Siamese government is to obtain tax revenue. In fact, the secret sale and the public sale are equally harmful to the people. Therefore, the benefits obtained from the public sale must not be increased, and the committee cannot encourage such benefits. Therefore, the US government absolutely opposes this proposal. Moreover, according to US law, the import of opium dregs is prohibited. When the convention was signed, opium-producing countries such as India, Turkey, Persia, Yugoslavia, etc. made great sacrifices. Now, the monopoly countries are using dregs to manufacture morphine to compete with raw opium, which is unfair to the producing countries. Finally, Mr. Fuller emphatically stated that the Siamese government's proposal is a gradual way to "abuse narcotics and poison the world" and sincerely hopes that all parties will pay attention to it. Geneva believes that the Siamese government's proposal has the support of the British and Japanese governments. (Central News Agency dispatch on the 21st)

The newspaper also said that China has a vast territory and difficult transportation, so it will not be possible for Nanjing to extend its power to the outer provinces in a short period of time. Now Nanjing apparently believes that the best policy is to establish order and revitalize industry and commerce in the Yangtze River basin, where its power can reach, and to avoid actions that oppress the outer provinces. Those who study the disturbances in their own country in the Middle Ages, observe Chinese events with patience, and feel excited that Nanjing is now following the right path. 南極發現陸地 5

From the Iceford Mountains

Extending to Infinity

Report from the American Expedition

The American Navy Rear Admiral Byrd-led Antarctic expedition’s radio report from Little America in Antarctica states that the expedition’s pilot, Harold June, recently explored by plane and discovered a large plateau that extends from the Iceford Mountains in the southeast direction to infinity, and is connected to the newly discovered Marie Byrd Land. According to previous rumors, Marie Byrd Land and the Iceford Iceberg extending over the land were a cluster of islands. This new discovery completely refutes the previous claim. Furthermore, this aerial exploration lasted for slightly less than eight hours, covering an area of 77,694 square kilometers on the new land. (20th Havas Dispatch)

British Prime Minister Declares to Parliament

Strengthening National Defense is Purely for Self-Defense

Unwavering in Commitment to Peaceful Efforts

Report on Indian Constitutional Reform Published

(London) Today, the House of Commons debated the King's Speech. Prime Minister MacDonald stated that the political situation abroad is extremely critical and need not be elaborated upon, so Britain must continue to strive to maintain world peace. MacDonald said, "The most important issue facing our country now is foreign relations. The confidence of various countries in the world has not increased in the past eighteen months. Therefore, we advocate continuing cooperation in Geneva, not only to show that we are a government that adheres to pacifism, but also to promote the greatest interests of our country." (20th National Dispatch)

(London) During the House of Commons discussion on the King's Declaration today, Labour Party leader Ramsay MacDonald delivered a speech stating, "The purpose of international discussions on various conventions is to oppose Germany. Germany is a great power. Since the European War, we have arbitrarily trampled on it. No country has been more devastated than Germany. Yet today, we are all fearful of Germany, deeply afraid of its actions." MacDonald's words are sufficient to prove that there are still people in Britain who recognize Germany as "a victim of the Treaty of Versailles." MacDonald also said, "The reason why the European situation is as it is today is largely due to the peace treaties after the European War. Now France, Germany, and even our country are constantly increasing armaments. Who are they defending against? I don't know. Can't these countries stop armaments and let their politicians use common sense to find a solution?" The Prime Minister, according to custom, answered the first question raised, but his declaration was very vague, and finally explained the rationale for Britain's strengthening of national defense. MacDonald also said that the British government advocates cooperating fully with the League of Nations, and will find ways to bring countries closer together whenever possible. Regarding the issue of disarmament, MacDonald said, "None of Britain's armaments are offensive or aggressive. We have proven this to the world, and none of the representatives of various countries in Geneva can deny it. Even if we strengthen armaments due to national defense needs, people in the world will never accuse Britain of wanting to increase its offensive military power to oppress unarmed countries. This is what I dare to say. Our intentions will be clearly expressed in the next military budget." (20th Havas Dispatch)

(London) The report of the Joint Committee on Indian Constitutional Reform, the content of which was eagerly awaited by the general public, was published this afternoon. This move represents the most arduous work in the history of the British Empire or the world regarding the study and revision of constitutions, and it has now been completed. The report advocates replacing the current centralized government system with a federal system for all of India, including autonomous units. The eleven provinces of India under British rule (two of which will be newly created) and the princely states of India will form a federal system. The princely states will join the federation voluntarily. The internal administrative system of the princely states and the relationship between the monarchs and monarchs outside the scope of the federation will not be changed. However, each province should expand the scope of its governance of its own affairs compared to the present. The majority of the administrative departments involving individuals, including law, order, and certain types of tax revenues and local taxes, will be the affairs to be handled by the provinces. The federal government will handle matters related to the entire Indian nation, such as currency and tax rules. Defense and foreign affairs will still be the direct responsibility of the Governor-General of India. Each province will have a legislative assembly, elected directly by voters. Voters account for about 14 percent of the population. Five of these provinces have upper and lower houses. The federal government has upper and lower houses, composed of those indirectly elected by the provinces and those appointed by the princely states. The parliaments of the federation and the provinces all stipulate seats for various ethnic minorities. The administrators of the federal and provincial governments are responsible to the parliament, the same as the British cabinet's system of responsibility to the parliament. (21st Reuters Dispatch)

Handling the Chaco Dispute

League of Nations Special Assembly Convenes

Mediation Committee Recommends

Paraguay Refuses to Accept

(Geneva) The League of Nations General Assembly convened an extraordinary session to handle the Chaco dispute. The meeting opened today, chaired by Czech representative Benes, Chairman of the Administrative Council. Benes delivered the opening speech, first paying tribute to the late King Alexander of Yugoslavia and French Foreign Minister Barthou. After a two-minute silence, Yugoslav Foreign Minister Jevtic thanked the League of Nations on behalf of the Yugoslav government, saying that the Marseille murder case affected international organizations (referring to the League of Nations) because both Alexander I and the late French Foreign Minister Barthou were enthusiastic defenders. French Foreign Minister Laval then spoke after Jevtic, praising the late monarch of Yugoslavia, saying that he was a great leader who "died on the battlefield of peace," and also said that he (Laval referring to himself) would strive to follow in Barthou's footsteps in order to complete his unfinished business. (20th Havas Dispatch)

(Geneva) The League of Nations extraordinary session for handling the Chaco dispute held its second meeting this morning. Discussions have already begun on the report and recommendations made by the Chaco Affairs Committee, chaired by Czech Ambassador to France Osusky. (21st Havas Dispatch)

Rio de Janeiro The Committee of the League of Nations General Assembly handling the Chaco dispute recommends resolving the dispute through mediation and arbitration. Prior to this, (1) military action should be stopped immediately, and the troops of both sides should remain on their existing front lines; (2) both sides should demobilize within a short period of time; (3) a demilitarized zone should be established; (4) the areas currently occupied by the belligerent countries should be maintained by the police. The above recommendations have been rejected by Paraguay. (20th Havas Dispatch)

Rio de Janeiro Paraguay replied to the League of Nations today, rejecting the League of Nations' proposal to end the Chaco War, but suggested starting with a ceasefire, disarmament, and security plan, and then resolving the dispute between Bolivia and Paraguay through reconciliation and arbitration. Although Paraguay's reply has not closed the door to negotiations, the League of Nations, which previously regarded the investigation committee's report as acceptable to both sides, so as to promote an early peace, is now greatly disappointed. If Bolivia accepts the League of Nations' proposal, Bolivia will be in an obviously advantageous position, because although the League of Nations' report approves the actions of some member states of the League of Nations in not allowing arms to be shipped into the belligerent countries, it advocates that if one of the belligerent countries accepts the League of Nations General Assembly's proposal and the other party does not accept it, then the country that has accepted the proposal can be exempted from the ban on arms supplies. (20th Reuters Dispatch)

Soviet Russia Announces Again

The Truth About the Stalemate in the Sino-Eastern Railway Negotiations

Japan Considers the Guarantee of Payment as an Insult

Opposes Submitting Disputes to Arbitration

(Moscow) Although there was a detailed report from TASS on October 31 regarding the truth about the Sino-Eastern Railway sale negotiations, at present, the Japanese and Manchurian newspapers are still reporting inaccurately on the progress of the negotiations. At the same time, internationally, it is generally believed that since the issue of the selling price has been resolved, what other selling conditions can delay the signing of the final agreement, which is strange. Therefore, TASS has collected other news about the truth of the negotiations from reliable sources in order to clarify the real cause of this delay.

Regarding certain selling conditions of the Sino-Eastern Railway, the Japanese side has been quite insistent on some of the Soviet Union's natural demands and is unwilling to agree, such as the reasonable demand for a guarantee of the funds allocated by the Soviet side, which is most obvious. This method is intended to erase the form of the "Manchukuo" debt guaranteed by the Japanese side. Unfortunately, since TASS published a detailed report on October 31, Japan has not changed its attitude on this important issue. The Soviet side believes that this is purely a commercial matter, while Japan has proposed the principle of "trust" in "Manchukuo" and is willing to assume the responsibility of "mediation" if "Manchukuo" has difficulties in payment. Not only that, but the Japanese side (especially the Japanese and Manchurian press) also regards the Soviet Union's demands as "distrust" of Japan and Manchukuo, and almost as an insult to Japan and Manchukuo. This has greatly surprised Moscow. They believe that when concluding such business, the use of a guarantee system is universally recognized. As for the current incident, this huge economic enterprise is sold by installments, and at the same time, the sovereignty of the railway will be transferred to the new owner from the time the agreement is signed. In such a situation, the customary requirement for a guarantee is natural. As for the issue of "distrust," it is even more absurd, because if the Soviet side does not trust the effectiveness of the Japanese guarantee, or does not affirm that Japan will never allow the debts guaranteed by the Japanese side to be defaulted on for its own benefit, then it will never ask Japan to provide a guarantee. The Soviet Union does so precisely because it assumes that the Japanese guarantee will ensure that the agreement can be implemented as usual.

At the same time, in order to consolidate the normal relations between the Soviet Union and Japan, it should be predicted that future disputes arising from the implementation of the sale agreement will not become the root cause of new conflicts between the two countries. In order to achieve this goal, the Soviet side has requested the establishment of arbitration in order to resolve future differences that may arise in the calculation of freight or road funds. At the same time, if impartial arbitrators cannot be determined, the Soviet Union suggests that these arbitrators should be appointed by foreign chambers of commerce with international prestige (such as the chambers of commerce of the United Kingdom and the United States). The name of this chamber of commerce should be noted in the agreement.

This issue is extremely important, because the Soviet Union allows the Japanese and Manchurian sides to use goods to pay two-thirds of the road price. At the same time, in order to satisfy the wishes of the Japanese side, the Soviet Union has agreed to expand the types of goods to include textiles, silk, tea, soybeans, rice, and other goods in addition to industrial machinery. However, the Japanese side has expressed opposition to the participation of foreign arbitrators. They suggested that the Japanese Ministry of Foreign Affairs or the Ministry of Commerce should appoint a person as the arbitrator. This suggestion was rejected because Japan cannot act as a completely unrelated "third party" in future disputes between the Soviet Union and Manchuria. Moreover, Japan is using this arbitration principle to resolve its economic disputes with other countries. For example, it is a signatory to the International Commercial Arbitration Agreement. Therefore, Japan's refusal to accept arbitration methods to resolve possible disputes between the Soviet Union and Manchuria is even more puzzling. The persistent attitude expressed by the Japanese side on the above issues is also attracting Moscow's attention, because in the notes addressed to Hirota by Yurenev on October 30, October 31, and November 6, the Soviet government made great concessions on other points of contention. We cannot point out all the important issues one by one here, but one thing that must be mentioned here is that the Japanese side has repeatedly canceled the points that were originally agreed upon, which has made it difficult for the negotiations to proceed. For example, on July 23, both parties agreed that once the negotiations were concluded, the retirement pay and support fees for the Sino-Eastern Railway employees would be allocated immediately. However, recently the Japanese suddenly announced that there was no such agreement before. The authorities here are most attentive to the fact that the attitudes of the Soviet and Japanese sides regarding the content of their respective wishes during the negotiations are very different. On the Soviet side, the following goals have been pursued: The Sino-Eastern Railway sale agreement, on the one hand, wants to permanently eliminate the possibility of using the Sino-Eastern Railway issue to make Soviet-Japanese relations tense, and at the same time, it must include guarantees to promote its smooth realization, thereby consolidating the political and economic relations between the two countries, which is conducive to world peace. Some of the suggestions from the Japanese side are the opposite. If these suggestions are adopted into the agreement, people will still be able to use the Sino-Eastern Railway issue as a source of conflict between Japan and the Soviet Union even after the sale of the Sino-Eastern Railway. This agreement was originally a tool for peace, but some Japanese can turn it into a weapon for future conflicts. Therefore, well-informed sources in the Soviet Union believe that the hope of giving this agreement the above-mentioned nature is in line with the interests of some Japanese people. If this is the case, then this agreement will be in obvious conflict with the good neighborly relations between the Soviet Union and Japan, so it will be incompatible with general peace. Therefore, the Soviet side sincerely hopes that the Japanese government can prove its good intentions and allow these negotiations to be completed satisfactorily, because this may not be a blessing for the Japanese. (21st TASS Dispatch)

Tense Cabinet Meeting in Japan

Discussing Budget Issues

Ministers of the Army and Navy Insist on Increasing Military Spending

(Tokyo) The Second Budget Cabinet Meeting was convened at the Prime Minister's residence at 1:40 PM on the 21st. First, Finance Minister Fujii reported on the outline of the Ministry of Finance's review of the supplementary requests from various ministries, stating that the total amount had reached 320 million yen, and the issuance of public bonds was limited. Not only must the market's ability to absorb be considered, but it must also be reviewed according to the policy of gradually reducing deficit public bonds. The total amount must not exceed 41 million yen. Various ministries have expressed dissatisfaction with this, but here we can only ask for understanding of the financial authorities' difficulties and to bear what must be borne. The military departments are the most dissatisfied with this review of supplementary requests, especially Army Minister Hayashi, who claimed that the Manchurian Incident has not yet normalized. At this critical international period of 1935-36, the military administration should make national defense preparation its necessity. Even if we understand the difficulties of the Ministry of Finance, this review cannot be recognized, and we hope to reconsider it. The Army Minister insisted on adding supplementary requests without any reduction with an extremely strong attitude, so the cabinet meeting became tense. Next, Navy Minister Osumi spoke, saying that the London Preparatory Disarmament Conference is still in progress, and the Navy believes that it is at a critical period, so this Ministry of Finance review cannot be recognized. The two ministers of the Army and Navy did not mention any figures, but took the recognition of the current situation as their starting point and expressed their unwillingness to compromise on the initial supplementary request. At this time, Finance Minister Fujii explained the current financial situation and repeatedly stated the aforementioned remarks, hoping that the military departments would retreat. Next, Interior Minister Goto requested additional funding for the current situation relief fund and disaster countermeasures budget. Education Minister Matsuda said that elementary schools are lacking food, and children's food expenses must be requested. Agriculture Minister Yamazaki also needed to add expenses for rural relief and rural revitalization. All ministers presented realistic situations and necessities, forcing the Finance Minister to repeat the reasons for the various reviews, and then Railways Minister Tokonami asked whether there was any room for easing the issuance of public bonds. The Finance Minister said that he would present his opinions on the tax increase plan in a short while, and then explained the limits of issuing public bonds based on the survey data. At this point, the cabinet meeting temporarily adjourned at 6:00 PM. After dinner, the meeting continued from 7:00 PM. (21st Japan Federation Electric)

Fang Zhimin's Remnant Troops

Failed to Invade Yushan

Four Committees of the Legislative Yuan

Review the Stamp Tax Law

(Nanjing) The Finance, Civil Law, Commercial Law, and Criminal Law Committees of the Legislative Yuan held a joint meeting on the morning of the 21st to review the new stamp tax law tax rates and penalty sections submitted by the Central Political Committee for reconsideration. Yu Ruliang, a representative from the Tax Administration, attended the meeting to explain. As a result of the review, the tax rate law, delivery notes, silver receipts, and bills are generally simplified, reducing the grading, on the one hand, to ensure that the tax revenue is not affected, and on the other hand, to facilitate the business community. Other items such as land deeds will be appropriately increased. As for the penalty section, the opinions presented by the Ministry of Finance are considered acceptable, and it is planned to impose a fine of five yuan for those with a fine of less than five yuan. Fines will not be imposed concurrently for more than two cases. After the regulations are sorted out, they will be submitted to the General Assembly for discussion. (21st Special Dispatch)

Banks Transporting Banknotes

Must Obtain Tax-Exempt Passports from the Military Department

(Nanjing) In addition to filling out passports issued by the Ministry of Finance, banks transporting banknotes must also apply to the Military Department for tax-exempt passports. Recently, the Military Department consulted the Ministry of Finance that in the future, when various banks apply for these passports, they should specify the words "National," "Provincial," and "Acting Treasury." As for whether commercial banks can continue to be issued, please the Ministry of Finance assess and decide. (21st Special Dispatch)

Although the tax rate has been drafted, it can only be fully determined after being reviewed and approved by the Legislative Yuan. Its meaning and purpose are to stabilize the market, and it is different in nature from the originally promulgated exchange tax and is not related to it. It will be implemented after it is announced. What Is Hoped For From the Central Rural Service Training Institute 6

By Ji

Recently, the Executive Yuan of the National Government held its 185th regular meeting. A resolution was made to establish a Central Rural Service Training Institute. It is planned to enroll an initial class of two to three hundred students. Eligibility is limited to university graduates. After being admitted, students will attend lectures at the institute for six months, and then be assigned to various experimental counties for a year of practical training, as an aid to promoting rural education. Such is the rough outline of the training institute's content. Its detailed plan and budget, however, must be approved by the Central Political Council before it can be established.

Our country is founded on agriculture. The majority of the nation's production comes from rural areas. It is not inappropriate to say that agriculture is the lifeblood of the nation. Therefore, if we want to talk about revitalizing the country and benefiting the people today, the most important plan is to improve agriculture and increase production. Only then will the nation's finances and people's livelihoods have the possibility of abundance. Our farmers stubbornly adhere to ancient methods. The simplicity of cultivation techniques and the degradation of both the quality and quantity of agricultural products prevent us from competing with advanced agricultural nations. This can be clearly seen in the annual surge in agricultural product imports. The depletion of national financial resources and the distress of the people's livelihoods are largely due to this. Many people advocate reclaiming wasteland and colonizing border areas. However, few have been seen who can truly implement relief and develop mature rural areas. As a result, ordinary farmers cannot maintain their fields and homes, and seek opportunities elsewhere, abandoning their land and not cultivating it, forming a nationwide phenomenon of declining agriculture. Although there are many ways to relieve rural areas, raising farmers' knowledge and promoting new planting methods are essential. In the past thirty years, those engaged in new education have known the importance of agricultural education, but few have personally promoted it. According to statistics from the Ministry of Education, in the 19th year of the Republic (1930), students in secondary vocational schools nationwide accounted for only a little over 6.7 percent, and agricultural students accounted for only a small portion of that. As for students in specialized schools and above in the 20th year of the Republic (1931), those studying agriculture and forestry accounted for only 3.2 percent of the total. This is the smallest number among all disciplines. However, from these fragmented statistics, it can be imagined that the number of people with scientific agricultural knowledge in the country is as rare as morning stars. In a country founded on agriculture, if agricultural education is so underdeveloped, can the economic future of the entire country be fortunate? Therefore, the urgent need to promote agricultural education in the future is a matter of course. The Executive Yuan's proposal to establish the Central Rural Service Training Institute is motivated by this, without a doubt. Although the establishment of the institute is still pending, the timeframe should not be far off. We not only optimistically look forward to its success, but also hope that it will be pragmatic and achieve results as soon as possible, and in a short period of time, become a major base for promoting rural education in experimental counties across the country.

What do we mean by being pragmatic? The small number of agricultural talents that our country has often do not use what they have learned. After completing their studies, they do not set foot in the fields, nor do they personally engage with beans and wheat. They only associate with the scholar-official class. Few of them can deeply engage with rural areas, change customs, engage in planting and cultivation, and serve as role models for farmers. Although their education focuses on production, they themselves do not participate in production. As a result, how can their impact on the production sector not be minimal? Since the government has high expectations for the Central Rural Service Training Institute, it should not merely be a way to find employment for a few university graduates, or a place for even fewer teaching staff to earn a living. It is conceivable that our earnest prayer for the establishment of the training institute lies in cultivating technical talents who deeply engage with rural areas, and absolutely preventing both staff and students from contracting the bad habits of the scholar-official class. Then, the benefits to rural education in various experimental counties will not be insignificant.

Serious Internal Strife in Austria

One Faction Shouts "Heimwehr Forever"

Another Faction Shouts "Schuschnigg Forever"

Large-Scale Police Suppression of Mutual Fighting

Innsbruck – The "Austrian Patriotic Front" is the only bulwark for the Austrian government to resist the Social Democratic Party and the National Socialist Party within the country. Internal strife has now occurred. The situation in Tyrol has been tense for the past few weeks. Today, the paramilitary group belonging to Chancellor Dr. Schuschnigg and the Home Guard had a serious conflict. The Home Guard, led by Vice-Chancellor Prince Starhemberg, suddenly shouted "Heimwehr Forever" at the supporters of the Chancellor to provoke them. The other side did not show weakness and shouted "Schuschnigg Forever." Thereupon, the Home Guard attacked and fought each other. Upon hearing the news, the authorities immediately dispatched a large number of police to the scene to suppress the situation. After much effort, the two factions were separated. Many people on both sides were injured, but none were seriously injured. The Home Guard threatened to retaliate, so armed police patrolled the entire city all day. Chancellor Schuschnigg, who had finished his talks with Mussolini in Rome, packed his bags and rushed back to his country upon hearing the news. (Reuter, 20th)

U.S. War Debts

(Washington) – The Treasury Department today, as usual, notified the war debt debtor countries that the debts owed to the United States are due on December 15th, totaling $154,729,976, not including previous arrears. The countries notified by the Treasury Department are Belgium, Czechoslovakia, Estonia, Finland, France, England, Hungary, Italy, Latvia, Lithuania, Poland, and Romania. Among them, only Finland has not previously defaulted. It is said that the Treasury Department does not expect the defaulting countries to pay on time, but this notification can show that the United States still adheres to its consistent policy, that is, war debts must be paid. Finland, which has never defaulted, today requested the U.S. Securities and Exchange Commission to issue bonds worth $10 million in the United States to repay part of its foreign debt. Given Finland's consistent attitude towards the war debt issue, it is generally believed that the committee will likely approve this request. (National Telegram, 20th)

Naval Negotiations Hanging by a Thread

Britain Tries to Make a Final Turnaround

Simon and Matsudaira Meet Again

British and American Plenary Meeting Tomorrow

Talks Leading to Political Issues Rejected by Japan

U.S. Emphasizes the Survival of Article 19 of the Washington Treaty

(London) – This morning, the Cabinet Council considered the serious status of the naval talks. British Foreign Secretary Simon will hold another meeting with Japanese Ambassador Matsudaira to determine if there is a way to reconcile the attitudes of Japan, Britain, and the United States. At the same time, it was agreed this afternoon that representatives of the British and American sides would hold a plenary meeting on a selected date, approximately November 23rd. (Reuter, 21st)

It is generally expected that President Roosevelt's reply to the British government will only involve cooperation between Britain and the United States to establish a new treaty. Britain and the United States will likely convene a meeting within a few months to lay the foundation for next summer's naval conference. At that time, France and Italy will be invited to participate. Next year's conference will definitely discuss multilateral treaties to replace the existing Washington Treaty. (Reuter, 21st)

(London) – Prime Minister MacDonald declared in the House of Commons today that he had hoped to report to the House on the current situation of the naval talks yesterday morning, but a new trend had emerged in the past twenty-four hours, and he intended to refrain from discussing it for the time being so that Parliament could hear the details after everything was completed. The House of Commons is currently engaged in debating the response to the King's address, which will take about five days to complete. Then, Foreign Secretary Simon will announce the progress of the naval talks in the House. (Reuter, 20th)

(London) – According to the opinions of members of the U.S. naval delegation, the naval talks are now over, with only handshakes and farewells remaining. It is heard that the Japanese and U.S. delegations will leave London in about a week or two. Today, the U.S. delegation stated that the United States does not want to discuss the clauses in the Washington Treaty on not setting up defensive works, because these clauses are only valuable if the original treaty exists. Thus, the last hope for a compromise in the naval talks was also dashed. (Reuter, 21st)

(London) – The situation of the naval talks may indirectly trigger all issues in the Far East. The Japanese representatives have repeatedly stated that even if the Washington Naval Treaty is declared abolished, the status quo of defensive works and naval bases in the Pacific, as stipulated in 1922, can still be maintained and should be maintained. The Japanese representatives have also repeatedly stated that the islands in the Pacific mandated to Japan for administration have not only not been fortified, but most of them cannot be equipped with defensive works. Chinese people in London have adopted a reserved and worried attitude towards this. They are deeply afraid that Japan is using secret means and said that the military equipment on the Pacific islands has been mentioned repeatedly, but Japan has not provided credible reasons for renewal. Chinese people also believe that the Washington Naval Treaty, the Kellogg-Briand Pact, the League of Nations Covenant, and all the clauses of the Washington Nine-Power Treaty are often regarded as waste paper, which is lamentable. As for the Americans, they say that the inability to set up defensive works on the Pacific mandated islands is stipulated by the mandate agreement and does not need to be discussed. The naval talks should continue on a technical level. (Havas, 20th)

The Theory of U.S.-Japan Equilibrium

Japan Seems to Have Made Such an Indication

(London) – Although the Japanese Ministry of Foreign Affairs denies the claim of a new Japanese proposal, the British delegation said at the fourth British-Japanese talks that Japan had advocated that "Britain has vast overseas territories, so it can recognize its possession of a high level of naval power, but it is necessary to possess the same naval power as the United States." However, Britain has, in principle, recognized the equal ratio of British and American naval power since 1922. If it agrees with the above-mentioned Japanese proposal, it will be contradictory and will fall into a difficult situation. (Dentsu, 20th)

(Tokyo) – Newspapers on November 19th carried the remarks of British Foreign Secretary Simon regarding the London Naval Talks. It was said that the British Foreign Secretary told reporters that Japan had adopted an attitude, thinking that Britain should build ships to a high level, and that the Japanese government did not see any reason why the U.S. Navy should be superior to the Japanese Navy. The British Foreign Secretary also said that the Japanese representatives had made it clear that even if Japan obtained naval equality, it would not want to build ships to the same level as Britain and the United States, but for the sake of face, Japan could never accept the 5:5:3 ratio again. This morning, the spokesperson of the Ministry of Foreign Affairs told foreign journalists that he did not believe that the British Foreign Secretary had made such remarks, because the delegations of various countries had an understanding that the content of the talks must be kept strictly confidential. (Reuter, 21st)

(London) – Colonel Iwashita of the Japanese delegation saw that the British authorities had published their views, saying that Japan's proposal for disarmament meant that the United States and Japan were equal and Britain was superior. In other words, it was the claim of an actual strength of 5:4:4, which caused a great uproar. Therefore, on the 20th, he issued the following statement to the foreign press corps, proposing that Britain could maintain a navy larger than Japan's. I have never heard the two plenipotentiaries Matsudaira and Yamamoto say this. Moreover, the preparatory meeting is still in its initial stage, and it is impossible to make a numerical proposal. This statement must be some kind of misunderstanding. (Dentsu, 21st)

(London) – Regarding the progress of the preparatory negotiations, various rumors have arisen here, and there is no consensus. It is said that Representative Matsudaira proposed a 5:4:4 ratio for the naval power of Britain, the United States, and Japan, and that he proposed to realize an equal annual plan with a limit of fifteen years. It is also widely rumored that Japan is advocating equilibrium with the United States and recognizing Japan's inferiority to Britain. Therefore, the Japanese delegation, the British government, and the U.S. delegation are all busy answering questions from the press corps, which is quite troublesome. (Nichi-Rengo, 21st)

Saito Makoto Writes

No Less Than a Warning to the Inside

Military Cliques Know Their Own Arrogance Very Well

Hoping for Some Achievement in the Naval Conference

(Washington) – The Christian Science Monitor today published an article by former Prime Minister Saito, attacking the aggression of Japan and other countries, saying that Japan will never have an aggressive policy. We must coexist in the world. If there is a warlike country, it will only increase the burden of various countries. He dared to say that the London Naval Conference must succeed in order to seek world peace. Anyone with proper thinking should know that a bankrupt naval competition cannot achieve anything. This trend will only make culture regress and foster hatred. People in the U.S. government have paid close attention to this article, but have not issued any criticism. At the same time, according to a report in the London Daily Telegraph, the U.S. side has notified the Japanese naval representatives that the U.S. government considers Article 19 of the Washington Treaty to be a major part of the treaty. If this treaty is no longer valid, then the clause regarding not placing defensive works in a certain location will naturally be invalid. (Reuter, 21st)

Boston – The Christian Science Monitor carried a conversation by former Japanese Prime Minister Saito, criticizing the Seiyukai for inciting Japan to oppose the extension of the naval treaty. Saito said that the Seiyukai was annoyed because Prime Minister Okada formed a cabinet and refused the manipulation of the majority party. It turned to support the Japanese military cliques. Saito was deeply concerned about the naval competition between Britain, the United States, and Japan, and believed that the Emperor could eventually subdue the military. He also said that he knew that the Emperor did not want Japan's navy to be unrestrained for a long time. Without the consent of the Prime Minister and the Cabinet, the Emperor would not want to approve new plans to expand the navy and increase taxes. (Kokumin, 20th)

(London) – General Saito, the former Japanese Prime Minister, published an article in the Christian Science Weekly, attacking the arrogant patriots of Japan and other countries, and advocated that the naval countries should establish an agreement to limit the number of warships. General Saito's article is no different from a solemn warning to the people of his own country, and has aroused the warmest and most pleasant impression in London, because Saito is a veteran in Japanese political circles, has held the most important positions for many years, and these remarks will inevitably cause a major shock. This is not denied by people on the Japanese side. As for the British and American people, although they have a good impression, they still adopt a reserved attitude. Responsible persons declared that if Saito made the remarks, it would be tantamount to suicide, but Saito's moderate, clear, and courageous attitude has long been known to the world when he first served as Governor-General of Korea and later as Prime Minister of Japan, so listening to these remarks is not surprising. Japanese military figures are now in key positions, and Saito's proposition has no hope of success, but it is impossible for responsible Japanese politicians to be unmoved by such wise remarks. Not to mention that, as far as we know, Saito's remarks are in line with the sentiments of some people in the Emperor's court. Therefore, although Saito is not directly involved in the current naval negotiations, his remarks will have an important impact on the naval talks, or generate a new meaning, which is possible. (Havas, 21st)

British Foreign Secretary Simon

Mentioned Political Issues

Matsudaira Directly Refused to Discuss

(London) – At the meeting on the 19th, Foreign Secretary Simon proposed to Japanese Representative Matsudaira to discuss political issues and asked Japan and Britain to take the same steps to implement the Far East policy and the China policy. The intention of the British proposal seems to be to renew the Nine-Power and Four-Power Treaties to ensure the security of China's territory and the peace of the Pacific. Representative Matsudaira replied that the discussion of political issues might cause disputes in the talks, and Japan would find it difficult to accept this proposal. (Nichi-Rengo, 20th)

(London) – The content of the proposal made by Foreign Secretary Simon to the Japanese representatives on the 19th to ensure the peace of the Pacific is as follows:

(1) Conclude a new treaty on China and the Pacific; (2) The new treaty guarantees the security of China's territory and confirms the maintenance of the freedom of North China; (3) Declare that when a naval building competition occurs, the political peace of the Pacific must be valued. (Nichi-Rengo, 20th)

Japanese Equal Rights

The United States Can Never Recognize

Davis Is Waiting Quietly for Instructions

(London) – The Japanese naval view has no possibility of being accepted by the United States, unless the Washington government fundamentally changes its attitude. The U.S. representatives are now asking the government for instructions. Before receiving instructions, they will continue to follow the original instructions and strongly oppose granting equal rights to Japan, regardless of how the equal rights are realized. Americans here believe that the Tokyo government's proposal for equal rights will eventually be formally rejected by the United States. (Havas, 20th)

British Prime Minister MacDonald

Postpones Reporting to the House of Commons

What Exactly Is the So-Called New Factor

(London) – Prime Minister MacDonald, when discussing the naval issue in the House of Commons this afternoon, said that he had originally intended to report to the House on the situation of the naval talks today, but a "new factor" had occurred yesterday, so he could not report it for the time being. What exactly does the Prime Minister mean by the so-called new factor? Perhaps the Japanese representatives have presented their views anew, or it is not yet known. At the Cabinet meeting tomorrow, Foreign Secretary Simon will review the results of the talks. Japanese people say that the naval equality requested by their country will be gradually realized over the years. The time limit needs to be negotiated. Japanese people also say that the naval talks should focus on the reduction of naval power, not on the increase. Therefore, what Japan advocates is not expanding the Japanese navy, but stipulating a common maximum amount. Any warships of Britain and the United States that exceed this maximum amount should be replaced. However, well-informed people in Britain answered the following points, namely (1) Up to now, Britain has not formally recognized the naval equality requested by Japan; (2) Britain can certainly agree to reduce the total tonnage of the British navy, but the number of warships cannot be reduced. (According to Britain's advocacy of a small-ship policy, the total tonnage can be reduced without reducing the number of ships.) British people have repeatedly stated that the number of warships set by the British Admiralty is essential for protecting British territory and maritime communications. For example, 15 armored ships, of which 6 are used for the European fleet, 6 are used for the Far East, and the remaining 3 are used for reserve, are all properly allocated and there is no excessive number. (According to the first naval preparatory talks this summer, the British representatives submitted the British naval plan to the U.S. representatives, which listed 15 armored ships and increased the number of cruisers from 40 to 70.) (Havas, 20th)

Japan's Strong Stance

Not Willing to Fall Behind in the Naval Building Competition

(London) – The spokesperson of the Japanese delegation, in view of rumors such as the U.S.-Japan equilibrium and British superiority theory and the introduction of the Pacific political issue theory, specifically stated to the press corps that Japan advocates realizing equal rights by setting a common maximum limit on possession, and a defense-oriented navy by reducing offensive weapons, and insists that it has nothing to do with political issues. Its statement is as follows:

We seek world naval power not for offensive purposes, so we advocate the reduction and abolition of battleships, aircraft carriers, and Class A cruisers, and the limited use of cruisers, destroyers, and submarines. Moreover, we must reduce the total possession of the entire fleet and jointly determine its maximum limit. If political issues are involved at that time, it will only complicate the meeting and will not help the matter. If the meeting breaks down, we are willing to avoid a naval building competition as much as possible, but if we are caught in an unconditional state and such a competition occurs, we are not willing to fall behind. (Dentsu, 21st)

(London) – This afternoon, Rear Admiral Yamamoto, the chief specialist of the Japanese delegation, declared to a representative of the British press, "If naval quantity restrictions cannot be stipulated on the basis of our proposal, then we cannot recognize any qualitative restrictions." (Havas, 20th)

Spain's Anti-Gas Preparations

Madrid – People here are now beginning to consider the possibility of defending against chemical warfare. A "Civil Protection School for Defense Against Chemical Warfare" has recently been established in the capital, and is presided over by an army major medical officer. In addition to theory, the course also includes practice in using anti-gas masks and respirators. 200 people in the capital have signed up for classes, with men and women each accounting for about half. (Havas, 21st)

U.S. Navy Secretary Orders

Strictly Prohibiting the Disclosure of Naval Secrets

The U.S. Is Often at a Disadvantage in Exchanging Information

Using This to Prevent Semi-Official Espionage Activities

(Washington) – Secretary of the Navy Swanson recently signed multiple orders, strictly prohibiting the disclosure of national defense information and preventing semi-official espionage activities. According to the Navy Department, there is currently a certain naval country that is unwilling to exchange information about the navy with the United States, saying that the internal affairs of the U.S. Navy can be known without going through the U.S. government, and there is no need to obtain it through exchange procedures. Now, when the London Naval Negotiations are underway, this situation will put the United States at a disadvantage, so the Navy Department has issued the above ban. The Navy Department will not make the original text of the ban public, but according to what is generally known, in the next annual report to Congress, all information that can reveal the United States' improvement of the navy will not be included, such as the construction of warships, aircraft, giant cannons, radio equipment, defensive mines, and the improvement methods of aircraft. The ban will also apply to government-owned shipyards and private shipyards that build warships for the Navy Department. Furthermore, foreigners are strictly prohibited from visiting the new 26,000-ton aircraft carrier "Yorktown" and the "Saratoga," which are under construction at Newport News Port near Norfolk, and the 13,000-ton aircraft carrier "Revenge," which recently cruised in South America and is now being renovated. In addition, a recent film fully revealed the driving skills of U.S. Navy bomber pilots, allowing foreign countries to understand the secrets, so navy films will also be strictly inspected. If foreigners want to visit U.S. warships or board naval ships for tours, they must obtain permission from the Chief of Naval Operations and the Director of the Bureau of Navigation in advance. The Navy Department originally had an anti-espionage intelligence agency, which was abolished after the Great War. It has now been restored in June of this year, and Navy Colonel Van Hook has been appointed as its director. (Havas, 20th)

Ba尔温's Remarks

Causing a Dutch Reaction

Foreign Minister Declares Loyalty to Traditional Policies

Dutch Territory Will Not Allow Others to Use It

Dutch Capital – British Privy Councilor Baldwin once declared in the House of Commons, "The British border is on the Rhine." Today, Foreign Minister Graaf issued a declaration on Baldwin's remarks, saying that the Netherlands has always been loyal to its traditional policies, and it is a mistake for outsiders to think that Dutch territory can be used for the defense of other countries. In conclusion, Mr. Graaf said that the Netherlands will never follow any country or group. (Havas, 20th)

Disputes Arise Again Over Disarmament

Austria Demands Equal Arms Rights

Clearly Showing Italy's Instigation

(London) – Disputes have arisen again in the disarmament situation, this time from Austria, because Austrian representative Flugel, who attended the disarmament conference, said today that if other countries increase their armaments, Austria will have no way to defend itself, so unless it first obtains equal rights, Austria will not be able to join any treaty. This is the first time Austria has publicly interfered in the disarmament issue. People in Vienna's political circles are paying close attention. It is generally believed that this must be related to the Rome Pact signed by Austria, Italy, and Hungary in March of this year, and is instigated by Italy, because Italy wants Austria to be strong. (Reuter, 21st)

Princess Marina Arrives in London

Princess Marina and others arrived in London this afternoon from Paris. The Duke of Kent greeted them at Dover, and the Emperor and Empress and the Crown Prince greeted them at Victoria Station. (Reuter, 21st)

Kunshan Bandits Arrested Immediately Upon Disembarking 7

The bandits Ding Changkai, Meng Qingyu, and others, three in total, arrived in Kunshan by train from Shanghai yesterday morning. They were filling their stomachs in a small teahouse next to the station. Detective Luo Zhen of the county's Public Security Bureau learned of this and immediately led detectives to arrest Ding and the other two. According to their confession, there were many accomplices who came by waterway and were scheduled to meet in Zhouxiang Town, and then carry out a robbery somewhere. Based on the confession, Detective Luo urgently led the police to the destination to wait, but the bandits were well-informed and already knew that Meng and others had been arrested. They fled back to Shanghai, so Detective Luo and others waited until evening without any results. The three bandits were then escorted to the bureau and transferred to the county for investigation.

Japanese Envoy Returned to Shanghai Yesterday

Speaking of this trip as merely an inspection of embassy affairs

Gratitude for the courteous hospitality of our officials along the way

A Central News Agency dispatch states that the Japanese Minister to China, Akira Ariyoshi, along with his counselors Arino, Secretary Yokokawa, and others, went to Peiping last month to inspect embassy affairs. Subsequently, they visited Jinan and Qingdao and arrived in Shanghai yesterday afternoon at 2 PM aboard the Dalian Steamship Company's Qingdao Maru from Qingdao. The local Japanese Consul-General and other Japanese residents went to welcome him. The Japanese envoy immediately received journalists aboard the ship to discuss the journey. Details are as follows:

Arrival in Shanghai

The Qingdao Maru docked at the Huangpu Wharf at 2 PM. The Public Concession Police and the Japanese Consulate Police dispatched armed constables to the port to maintain security. Mrs. Ariyoshi, Counselor Horiuchi of the Japanese Embassy, Consul-General Ishii, Director of the Intelligence Department Ashino Hiroshi, Police Chief Hanari, Commander of the Japanese Naval Landing Forces Sugibane, and local Japanese residents all arrived to welcome him. Commissioner Wang Changchun of the Shanghai Municipal Government also arrived to welcome him. After arriving in Shanghai, the Japanese envoy shook hands with all the welcoming personnel, then disembarked, got into a car, and went directly to his residence on Rue Bisson to rest.

Remarks by the Japanese Envoy

The Japanese envoy met with journalists aboard the ship and made the following remarks: "This trip north was to inspect embassy affairs. On the return journey, I toured Jinan, Qingdao, and other places. I am very grateful for the courteous hospitality of the Chinese officials along the way. In Peiping, I met with Chairman Huang of the Political Affairs Reorganization Committee several times, but these were merely private social engagements and did not involve discussions on Sino-Japanese issues. Regarding the mutual exchange of ambassadors between China and Japan, there was a lot of talk about it several years ago. I do not know whether the Japanese government will bring it up again due to the promotion of the Chinese Minister to Italy. The addition of a Counselor to the Japanese Embassy in China is still under consideration." As for the American telegram regarding the convening of a Pacific Conference, Ariyoshi did not wish to comment, stating only that he did not know the details of this news because he was traveling.

Antiquities in Shanghai

Continued Inventory Yesterday

Shu Chushi and others all came to supervise the process

The antiquities from the Palace Museum stored in Shanghai began to be inventoried on the 20th of this month and continued yesterday. Two groups worked each morning and afternoon. Surveillance committee members Shu Chushi, attendant Xue Ye, and Ouyang Daoda, director of the Shanghai office, all arrived on time to supervise the work. Yesterday morning and afternoon, a total of eleven boxes of porcelain, four boxes of jade, and one box of miscellaneous items transported from the Antiquities Museum were inventoried. The box numbers were originally classified and numbered by the Antiquities Museum. For the convenience of registration, a general number was brushed on all four sides of the box, starting with Shanghai Character Number One for the boxes being inventoried this time, to ensure consistency. Boxes not completely inventoried by one group were sealed by the surveillance committee members for the next group to continue inventorying, to ensure thoroughness.

Sino-British Boxer Indemnity Committee

Finance Committee Met Yesterday

Approved the Jiangsu Provincial Government's Loan for Purchasing Fishing Vessels, etc.

Scheduled to Convene a Plenary Board Meeting in Shanghai

The Finance Committee of the Sino-British Boxer Indemnity Committee held a meeting at 4:30 PM yesterday in the meeting room of the British Bank, reviewed and approved important cases such as Jiangsu Province borrowing more than one million to purchase fishing vessels. Details are as follows:

Attending Directors

The Sino-British directors present yesterday included Chen Qicai, Masier, Jing En, Zeng Rongpu, and Song Ziliang. Those attending as observers were Shen Baixian, Director of the Jiangsu Construction Department, Zheng Baozhi, Secretary of the Board of Directors, and seven others. Chen Qicai presided and Zheng Baozhi recorded.

Discussion of Cases

After the meeting began, the chairman introduced Shen Baixian, Director of the Jiangsu Construction Department, who reported on the plan to borrow more than one million in Boxer Indemnity funds to purchase fishing vessels and the completion of the guarantee. The committee unanimously reviewed and approved the plan. Next, they discussed the case of the Ministry of Industry and the Zhejiang Provincial Government borrowing more than one million in Boxer Indemnity funds to build a paper mill in Wenxi, Zhejiang. Because Zeng Yangfu, Director of the Zhejiang Construction Department, was not present, no decision was made, but it is generally considered that there is no problem and it is expected to be approved at the general meeting. Then, other important cases were discussed, which will not be announced for the time being because they need to be submitted to the general meeting for approval. The meeting adjourned at 6:30 PM.

Board Meeting

The committee is scheduled to hold an executive meeting on Saturday and a general meeting of the Sino-British Boxer Indemnity Committee next Monday at the Bankers' Club on Hong Kong Road. At that time, it will, based on the finance committee’s review report, approve the Jiangsu Province borrowing Boxer Indemnity funds to purchase fishing vessels.

China Merchants Steam Navigation Company

Suspends Overseas Routes

Puan Wheel Returned to the Ministry of Navy

Haiheng Wheel Expected to Arrive in Shanghai at the End of the Month

A Central News Agency dispatch states that the state-run China Merchants Steam Navigation Company's Puan Wheel was initially jointly operated with the Ministry of Navy, remodeled into a passenger ship, and traveled between Shanghai and Qingdao, also visiting Putuo. Later, after the contract expired, China Merchants Steam Navigation Company leased and operated it. Recently, the company received an order from the Ministry of Communications to open overseas routes. It was originally intended to repair the ship and sail between Shanghai and Southeast Asia, but due to the company's financial difficulties and uncertainty about the business after opening overseas routes, the plan was temporarily abandoned. The company has canceled the expiring contract with the Ministry of Navy and sent personnel to remove all equipment from the ship and return it to the Ministry of Navy. In addition, the Haiheng Wheel, which the company ordered to be built in England, has already completed its construction and sailed to China for delivery, following the Haiyuan Wheel. It is expected to arrive at the port around the 27th or 28th of this month.

Copper and Iron Machinery Association

Efforts to Promote Sales of Domestic Products

A Stimulant in a Period of Depressed Imports

Since the September 18th Incident, the Copper and Iron Machinery Association of this city has been extremely earnest about the work of resisting imported goods. With the unity of everyone, after the January 28th Incident, factories voluntarily concentrated and sealed up foreign iron. Last summer, in order to support our country's only Liukegou domestic pig iron, they loudly appealed to help promote sales, and did their best to advise iron merchants and users. As a result, the sales of domestic iron increased greatly, and foreign iron almost disappeared from the market. The Shanghai Chamber of Commerce, in order to commend their exemplary role, presented a plaque inscribed with "Keeping Faith" to commemorate them. However, with the passage of time, people became complacent. Recently, it was discovered that some unscrupulous people were selling foreign iron for personal gain, and some members of the industry also violated the agreement and privately imported foreign iron. In order to consolidate the foundation of resisting goods and to prevent domestic iron from stagnating, which would affect future national defense plans, the enthusiastic members of the association have renewed their spirits and continued to work hard. On the one hand, they have sent personnel to conduct strict investigations, and on the other hand, they have notified all members to adhere to their original intentions and carry them through to the end. They have also sent a letter to the Iron Industry Association to assist in the process. It is expected that after a period of solid work, the results will be even more impressive. The original text of the association's notice to members is as follows: Notice: This association has always believed that the rise and fall of domestic iron has a long-term relationship with the rise and fall of national defense, and a short-term impact on the personal interests of this industry. Therefore, last year, we organized an office to promote the sale of domestic iron, striving to promote domestic goods and resist foreign aggression. Thanks to the enthusiastic patriotism of our colleagues and their concerted support, we have achieved remarkable results over the past year. The Municipal Chamber of Commerce has specially awarded a plaque to commend us, which is not only the glory of this association in promoting domestic goods, but also the spirit of our colleagues who understand the great righteousness and are united in saving the country. We should encourage ourselves to do even better and persevere to the end. However, we are afraid that with the passage of time, people will become complacent, or that some unscrupulous people will forget righteousness for profit and privately import foreign goods, becoming a scourge to our colleagues. We must once again carry out strict rectification and reaffirm the old agreement. Therefore, this notice is issued, urging colleagues to adhere to their original intentions, uphold the previous agreement, and not slacken in the slightest. We must work together with this association, fight to the end, and the future of saving the country depends on it. We also plan to send personnel to continue to conduct strict investigations in various factories. If it is found that foreign goods have been privately imported, in addition to being dealt with in accordance with the original penalty rules, we must also publish it in the newspapers for public opinion to censure. We hope that you will cherish your reputation and not be abandoned by the Chinese people or despised by foreigners. This is our sincere hope. This notice is hereby issued, and we hope you will take note.

Lawyers Association Sends Letter to French Consul-General

To Stop the Police Abusing Their Power

Police Department Sends Letter to the Court to Seal Up Shops

Interfering with Lawyers Handling Cases According to Law

Which is Damage to the Agreement Establishing Chinese Courts in the French Concession

The Shanghai Lawyers Association sent a letter yesterday to Mr. Meyrier, the French Consul-General in Shanghai, which stated: "We are writing to inform you that, according to a letter from member Ye Changyi, he was entrusted on November 5 of this year to handle the liquidation of Rentai Chang Kee and Andong Socks Factory. The two shops were not open for business that day, and the member sent staff to guard the goods in the shops and posted liquidation notices on the doors of the two shops, in addition to publishing them in Shen and Xin Bao, to inform creditors to register according to law. Unexpectedly, the French police suddenly sent detectives at 10 AM to arrest the person guarding the goods in Rentai Chang Kee and detained him for six hours. At the same time, they allowed many people claiming to be creditors to enter and leave the shop to guard it. When the member learned of this at 7 PM, he realized that if the above actions were true, he would be responsible for any loss of goods in the shop. Therefore, he drove to the shop to investigate, but found that there were police guarding both shop entrances, preventing him from entering. The member told them that he was the liquidator and showed them his badge and calling card, but to no avail. Therefore, he went to the police station to negotiate and asked them to withdraw the police, but was refused. They said that they could only withdraw after the court sealed up the shop. On the 6th of this month, the French Concession Police Department suddenly sent an official letter to the Second Special District Local Court requesting the seal up. Since then, the member has been unable to check the goods in the shop and has been unable to carry out the liquidation and convene the proceedings. Liquidating the accounts of a shop is purely a civil matter and has nothing to do with the police. However, they have arrested people and prohibited the liquidator from performing his duties. On the contrary, they have allowed many unnamed people claiming to be creditors to enter and leave the shop at will. This is undoubtedly an abuse of power and interference in the judiciary. As the above two shops have entrusted a liquidator to declare liquidation according to law, everything concerning the shop should be subject to legal裁制. How can the police openly advocate to the court to issue a seal up? Therefore, this behavior of the police is not only a violation of the agreement, but also an interference in the judiciary and an infringement on private rights. If this trend continues, the people will lose the protection of the law. Therefore, we have reported the beginning and end of the matter in detail to the meeting and hope that you will raise it for discussion and advocate for correction." Based on this, it is found that lawyers are entrusted by the parties to handle shop liquidation and are performing their duties according to law, free from interference by third parties. However, the governing police station, without examining the facts, abused its power and sent police to prohibit lawyers from exercising their duties, which is not in accordance with the law. Moreover, the Police Department sent a letter to the Second Special District Local Court requesting the seal up of the shop, which is even more illegal. The court's seal up disposition in civil matters is a preservation procedure or compulsory execution applied to the defendant based on the plaintiff's or the executor's application. The Police Department is neither a civil plaintiff nor an executor, and has no right to act on its behalf. In summary, this not only has the suspicion of interfering in the judiciary, but also should bear the responsibility for damaging the agreement establishing Chinese courts in the French Concession. After the joint meeting of the 183rd Executive and Supervisory Committee of this association, it was decided that a letter should be sent to your Consul-General to stop and correct the matter. Accordingly, we send this letter and hope that you will investigate and stop the aforementioned illegal and abusive behavior of the police station and the Police Department, so as to strengthen diplomatic relations and give a reply on the handling of the matter. This is our sincere hope. Signed, the Standing Committee of the Shanghai Lawyers Association, to Mr. Meyrier, French Consul-General in Shanghai.

Foreign Exchange Stabilization Committee

Fund of 10 Million Yuan

Silver Transported to Coastal Areas for Re-export

Efforts are Being Made by the Ministry of Finance to Stop It

A Central News Agency dispatch states that a member of the Foreign Exchange Stabilization Committee told reporters that the committee's fund of 10 million yuan, with 4 million yuan each from the Central Bank and the Bank of China and 2 million yuan from the Bank of Communications, is not prepaid but paid on demand. On the morning of the 19th, the committee announced the equalization tax at 7.75%. It was also said that since the implementation of the silver tax increase, silver exports have been reduced to a very small number, but there is more flow to various ports in the interior. Silver transported to various coastal ports is inevitably smuggled out, and the Ministry of Finance is now trying to prevent it.

Zhejiang Relief Committee

Sends Personnel to Various Counties for Relief Distribution

Administrative Yuan Disallows Additional Levy of Transportation Surtax

Tax Exemption for Relief Grain Requires Review and Transmission by the Relief Committee

The Zhejiang Relief Committee sent a letter to the Jiaxu All-Zhejiang Relief Committee yesterday to distribute relief directors in various counties and levy additional transportation surtax for the relief of the Zhejiang disaster. It was not approved. Details are as follows:

Letter from the Relief Committee to the Jiaxu Committee: The Zhejiang Relief Committee's letter to the Jiaxu Committee states that the drought disaster in Zhejiang this year has been severe. The committee, together with the Civil Affairs and Finance Departments, sent personnel to various counties to investigate and reported to the provincial government for review. Although the investigation and reporting have not yet been completed, the winter season has arrived, and the disaster victims are suffering from hunger and cold and are in dire need of food. It is imperative to select the counties most severely affected by the disaster and conduct winter relief distribution first to provide assistance. The counties with lighter disasters will be included in the work relief plan and handled together. It is found that Hai'ning and Haiyan, two counties severely affected by the disaster, have already had personnel sent by the Shanghai Chinese Jisheng Society, and Jiaxing, Chongde, Tongxiang, Shangyu, Shengxian, and Xinchang have had personnel sent by your committee to investigate and distribute relief separately. In addition, the committee has selected experienced relief personnel to be responsible for investigating and distributing winter relief in 30 counties including Wuxing. In addition to submitting a request to the provincial government for additional appointments and sending separate notices, a list of the names of the directors of relief distribution is enclosed for your information. Furthermore, Jiangshan, Changshan, Kaihua, and Sui'an counties have been hit by both drought and banditry, and the disaster situation is particularly severe. Also, Fuyang County is a paper-producing area, and according to the county magistrate's application, relief funds should be allocated to maintain the paper mill. Hangzhou City belongs to the provincial area, and the provincial granary has already started distributing porridge in advance, which can be used to provide relief to disaster victims. It is proposed to submit a separate case for review. Therefore, it is not included in the list of counties allocated for relief distribution this time. This is combined and clarified. Chairman Lu Bichou of the Zhejiang Relief Committee, Standing Committee members Zhang Zaiyang, Feng Xueshu, Jin Changshun, and Qian Wenxuan.

District Directors: The relief directors assigned to various counties by the Zhejiang Relief Committee are recorded as follows: (1) Gu Zongkuang: Wukang, Yuhang, Deqing. (2) Wu Sanqing: Wuxing, Changxing, Dongyang. (3) Jin Da: Anji, Xiaofeng. (4) Shen Guilin: Hang County, Yuqian, Lin'an, Tonglu. (5) Wang Hao: Fenshui, Xindeng. (6) Wu Wenqi: Jiande, Pujiang, Chun'an, Shouchang. (7) Pan Junlin: Yongkang, Wuyi. (8) Tian Yudong: Tiantai, Xianju. (8) Lu Zhinan: Jinhua, Lanxi, Qu County, Longyou. (10) Shen Zaichuan: Xuanping, Jinyun, Songyang. (11) Shen Pei'an: Xiao'an.

Transportation Surtax: According to the Great Letter, Cheng Hongjun and others in Tongxiang telegraphed requesting to levy a traffic surtax for disaster relief, citing previous cases. This request has been presented to the provincial government and forwarded to the Executive Yuan, which has instructed that it should not be approved. It is truly beyond our ability to meet the need. The Hangzhou-Jiangshan Railway disaster relief surtax was initiated by this province, and there is said to be approval for a trial, but no order has been received from the provincial government. The letter is hereby returned for your information.

Tax-Exempt Relief Goods: The Zhejiang Provincial Government replied to the relief committee, stating that the committee's previous telegram requesting that the Ministry of Finance be consulted to exempt import taxes on relief grain had been forwarded and replied to by telegram. Now, the Ministry of Finance's Guanzi No. 9612 replied, stating that the provincial government's Minzi No. 2989 requested that the Jiaxu All-Zhejiang Relief Committee plans to purchase 100,000 shi of relief grain from Nanyang, Siam, Java, and other places, and transport it in batches to Shanghai and then to various counties in the interior severely affected by the disaster for winter and spring relief. It requested that import taxes be exempted to benefit the poor. According to the situation, the request was forwarded to the department for review and reply. According to regulations, tax exemption for disaster relief goods should be requested by the relief committee and reviewed and transmitted by the relief committee to the ministry for review and approval. This is hereby replied and you are requested to inform us. Chairman Lu Dipin.

Shandong Tobacco-Producing Area

Dai Gengxin Returns from Inspection

Says the Future is Quite Promising

Dai Gengxin, Chairman of the Huacheng Tobacco Company, along with three American tobacco merchants including William Henney, went to the tobacco-producing areas of Huangqibao, Ershilibao, Tanjia, Fangzi, Yangjiazhuang, and Xindian, all under the jurisdiction of Qingzhou, Shandong, to inspect the tobacco produced and the conditions of the rural areas. The group returned to Shanghai the day before yesterday (20th). Mr. Dai gave a speech yesterday, saying that the tobacco leaves used by the Chinese cigarette industry are mostly from Qingzhou, Shandong, and Xuzhou, Henan. This is because the tobacco leaves in these two places are the same type as those produced in Florida and Virginia in the United States, and the Qingzhou tobacco leaves taste more mellow. Therefore, the tobacco companies in this city go to these two places every autumn to collect them, and the quantity is very large. If the tobacco leaves produced in our country can be transported overseas, there will definitely be opportunities for sales. (I, Dai, claimed) When I was in Europe last time, I discussed this idea with various European merchants, and they expressed great sympathy. Now, the samples of tobacco leaves have been sent there. This time, William Henney, chairman of the American Tobacco Company, came to China in return, and also believes that Chinese tobacco leaves can be sold overseas. However, foreigners are afraid that Chinese farmers have improper behaviors, such as mixing sand and mud or soaking them in water, as was the case with agricultural products exported in the past. Therefore, they cannot be trusted by foreigners, which is regrettable. This time, going to various leaf-producing areas with Zhang Lingheng and others can gain insight into the conditions of rural areas, the behavior of farmers, and the quality of tobacco leaves in our country. This trip is very satisfactory. I have met with people from all walks of life in various places, and they all believe that the transportation and sale of tobacco leaves overseas will be very beneficial to the rural economy in the country. The welcome from various places was very lively, and the protection from the government was very thorough, which is especially appreciated. When I was in Jinan, I met with bankers and asked them to set up more offices in rural areas to lend money to farmers to help the rural areas. Farmers who grow tobacco leaves need to use soybean cake for irrigation and burn coal for baking, so the cost is greater than for other crops, and the profit is also large. Reports that loans were borrowed from Shanghai banks for the harvest of tobacco leaves are inaccurate. Chinese people established the China Tobacco Leaf Company in Qingdao in 1920. I am honored to be the chairman of the board, and I registered with the Ministry of Industry early on and built factories, warehouses, and leaf-baking machines to specialize in the selection of domestic tobacco leaves, with remarkable results. This time, I went with American tobacco giants to study and research, and the soil in Shandong is fertile and most suitable for growing tobacco leaves. Moreover, the tobacco leaves produced have continued to improve compared to the past. The American merchants also believe that they are not much different from those produced in the United States. If we can continue to study gradually to seek improvement, there is great hope. I have suggested to Zhang Youshan, Director of the Construction Department of Shandong Province, to supervise farmers to cultivate, and he has greatly appreciated it. Director Zhang attaches great importance to the promotion of tobacco leaf production as a major product of Shandong Province and believes that it is essential to promote farmers' production. This will not only allow domestic tobacco factories to collect as much as possible, but also seek to sell it overseas, occupy a superior position in international trade, and prevent it from declining permanently. The economy of Shandong farmers will inevitably improve day by day.
